     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_residences">Faculty residences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Faculty residences">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>One of the benefits of being a Stanford faculty member is the &quot;Faculty Ghetto&quot;, where faculty members can live within walking or biking distance of campus. The Faculty Ghetto is composed of land owned entirely by Stanford. Similar to a <a href="/wiki/Condominium" title="Condominium">condominium</a>, the houses can be bought and sold but the land under the houses is rented on a 99-year lease. Houses in the &quot;Ghetto&quot; appreciate and depreciate, but not as rapidly as overall <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> values. However, it remains an expensive area in which to own property, and the average price of single-family homes on campus is actually higher than in Palo Alto. Stanford itself enjoys the rapid capital gains of Silicon Valley landowners, although by the terms of its founding the university cannot sell the land.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-main_campus">Non-main campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Non-main campus">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Stanford currently operates or intends to operate in various locations outside of its main campus.</p> 
     <p>On the founding grant but away from the main campus:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jasper_Ridge_Biological_Preserve" title="Jasper Ridge Biological Preserve">Jasper Ridge Biological Preserve</a> is a 1,200-acre (490&nbsp;ha) natural reserve owned by the university and used by wildlife biologists for research, located south of the main campus.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/SLAC_National_Accelerator_Laboratory" title="SLAC National Accelerator Laboratory">SLAC National Accelerator Laboratory</a> is a facility located west of main campus and originally owned by Stanford but now operated by the university for the Department of Energy. It contains the longest <a href="/wiki/Linear_particle_accelerator" title="Linear particle accelerator">linear particle accelerator</a> in the world, 2 miles (3.2&nbsp;km) on 426 acres (172&nbsp;ha) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Off the founding grant:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Hopkins_Marine_Station" title="Hopkins Marine Station">Hopkins Marine Station</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Grove,_California" title="Pacific Grove, California">Pacific Grove</a>, California, is a <a href="/wiki/Marine_biology" title="Marine biology">marine biology</a> research center owned by the university since 1892.</li> 
      <li>Study abroad locations: unlike typical <a href="/wiki/Student_exchange_program" title="Student exchange program">study abroad</a> programs, Stanford itself operates in locations around the globe; thus, each location, which ranges from <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, has Stanford faculty-in-residence and staff in addition to students, creating a &quot;mini Stanford.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Locations in development:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Redwood City: in 2005, the university purchased a small, 35-acre (14&nbsp;ha) campus in Midpoint Technology Park intended for staff offices, although it remains undeveloped.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>China: the university is currently building a small campus for researchers and students in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Peking_University" title="Peking University">Peking University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The university also has its own golf course and a seasonal lake (<a href="/wiki/Lake_Lagunita" title="Lake Lagunita">Lake Lagunita</a>, actually an irrigation reservoir), both home to the vulnerable <a href="/wiki/California_Tiger_Salamander" title="California Tiger Salamander" class="mw-redirect">California Tiger Salamander</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Lagunita" title="Lake Lagunita">Lake Lagunita</a> is often dry now, but the university has no plans to artificially fill it.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;"> 
      <div class="thumbinner"> 
       <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lakelag.jpg" class="image" title="Lake Lagunita in early spring; the Dish is visible in the foothills behind the lake."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Lakelag.jpg/800px-Lakelag.jpg" width="800" height="183" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Lakelag.jpg/1200px-Lakelag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Lakelag.jpg/1600px-Lakelag.jpg 2x" /></a>
       </div> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lakelag.jpg" title="Enlarge"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         <i>Lake Lagunita in early spring; the Dish is visible in the foothills behind the lake.</i>
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2011, the university also participated in the bidding for applied science campus in New York City but finally abandoned the project at the end of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_organization">Administration and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Administration and organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Stanford University is a tax-exempt <a href="/wiki/Corporate_trust" title="Corporate trust">corporate trust</a> owned and governed by a privately appointed 35-member <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Trustees" title="Board of Trustees" class="mw-redirect">Board of Trustees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FG_facts_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG_facts-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Trustees serve five-year terms (not more than two consecutive terms) and meet five times annually.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> A new trustee is chosen by the remaining Trustees by ballot.<sup id="cite_ref-FoundingGrant_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoundingGrant-25"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The Stanford trustees also oversee the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Research_Park" title="Stanford Research Park">Stanford Research Park</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Shopping_Center" title="Stanford Shopping Center">Stanford Shopping Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Iris_%26_B._Gerald_Cantor_Center_for_Visual_Arts" title="Iris &amp; B. Gerald Cantor Center for Visual Arts">Cantor Center for Visual Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_Medical_Center" title="Stanford University Medical Center">Stanford University Medical Center</a>, and many associated medical facilities (including the <a href="/wiki/Lucile_Packard_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Lucile Packard Children's Hospital">Lucile Packard Children's Hospital</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FG_facts_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG_facts-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Board appoints a President to serve as the chief executive officer of the university and prescribe the duties of professors and course of study, manage financial and business affairs, and appoint nine vice presidents.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_L._Hennessy" title="John L. Hennessy">John L. Hennessy</a> was appointed the 10th President of the University in October 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The Provost is the chief academic and budget officer, to whom the deans of each of the seven schools report.<sup id="cite_ref-Provost_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Provost-79"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Etchemendy" title="John Etchemendy">John Etchemendy</a> was named the 12th Provost in September 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is organized into seven schools: <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_School_of_Humanities_and_Sciences" title="Stanford University School of Humanities and Sciences">School of Humanities and Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_School_of_Engineering" title="Stanford University School of Engineering">School of Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_School_of_Earth_Sciences" title="Stanford University School of Earth Sciences">School of Earth Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Graduate_School_of_Education" title="Stanford Graduate School of Education">School of Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Graduate_School_of_Business" title="Stanford Graduate School of Business">Graduate School of Business</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Law_School" title="Stanford Law School">Stanford Law School</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_School_of_Medicine" title="Stanford University School of Medicine">Stanford University School of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Provost_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Provost-79"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The powers and authority of the faculty are vested in the Academic Council, which is made up of tenure and non-tenure line faculty, research faculty, senior fellows in some policy centers and institutes, the president of the university, and some other academic administrators, but most matters are handled by the Faculty Senate, made up of 55 elected representatives of the faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Associated_Students_of_Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Associated Students of Stanford University (page does not exist)">Associated Students of Stanford University</a> (ASSU) is the student government for Stanford University and all registered students are members.<sup id="cite_ref-ASSU_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASSU-82"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Its elected leadership consists of the Undergraduate Senate elected by the undergraduate students, the Graduate Student Council elected by the graduate students, and the President and Vice President elected as a <a href="/wiki/Ticket_(election)" title="Ticket (election)">ticket</a> by the entire student body.<sup id="cite_ref-ASSU_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASSU-82"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Stanford is the beneficiary of a special clause in the <a href="/wiki/California_Constitution" title="California Constitution" class="mw-redirect">California Constitution</a>, which explicitly exempts Stanford property from taxation so long as the property is used for educational purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Endowment_and_fundraising">Endowment and fundraising</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Endowment and fundraising">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university's <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">endowment</a>, managed by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_Management_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stanford Management Company (page does not exist)">Stanford Management Company</a>, was valued at $17.2 billion in 2008 and had achieved an annualized rate of return of 15.1% since 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-FG_facts_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FG_facts-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The endowment fell 25% in 2009 as a result of the late-2000s recession, but posted gains of 14.4% in 2010 and 22.4% in 2011, when it was valued at $16.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Stanford has been the top fundraising university in the United States for several years. It raised $911 million in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> $832 million in 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> $785 million in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> $640 million in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> $599 million in 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> $709 million in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-finances_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finances-91"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> and $1.035 billion in 2012, becoming the first school to raise more than a billion dollars in a year.<sup id="cite_ref-Record_Fundraising_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Record_Fundraising-92"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2006 President Hennessy launched a five-year campaign called the Stanford Challenge, which reached its $4.3 billion fundraising goal in 2009, two years ahead of time, but continued fundraising for the duration of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> It concluded on December 31, 2011, having raised a total of $6.23 billion and breaking the previous campaign fundraising record of $3.88 billion held by Yale.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> Specifically, the campaign raised $253.7 million for undergraduate financial aid, as well as $2.33 billion for its initiative in &quot;Seeking Solutions&quot; to global problems, $1.61 billion for &quot;Educating Leaders&quot; by improving K-12 education, and $2.11 billion for &quot;Foundation of Excellence&quot; aimed at providing academic support for Stanford students and faculty. Funds supported 366 new fellowships for graduate students, 139 new endowed chairs for faculty, and 38 new or renovated buildings. Over 10,000 volunteers helped in raising 560,000 gifts from more than 166,000 donors.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg/220px-Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg" width="220" height="337" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg/330px-Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg/440px-Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_University_Walkway_Panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Walkway to the School of Education, near the Quad
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Stanford University is a large, highly residential research university with a majority of enrollments coming from graduate and professional students.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-96"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> The full-time, four-year undergraduate program is classified as &quot;more selective, lower transfer-in&quot; and has an arts and sciences focus with high graduate student coexistence.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-96"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford University is accredited by the <a href="/wiki/Western_Association_of_Schools_and_Colleges" title="Western Association of Schools and Colleges">Western Association of Schools and Colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> Full-time undergraduate tuition was $38,700 for 2010-2011.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The schools of Humanities and Sciences (27 departments), Engineering (9 departments), and Earth Sciences (4 departments) have both graduate and undergraduate programs while the schools of Law, Medicine, and Education and the Graduate School of Business have graduate programs only.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford follows a quarter system with Autumn quarter usually starting in late September and Spring Quarter ending in early June.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faculty_and_staff">Faculty and staff</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Faculty and staff">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Stanford's current community of scholars includes:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>19 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> laureates;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>152 members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>95 members of <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Engineering" title="National Academy of Engineering">National Academy of Engineering</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>66 members of <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>268 members of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>18 recipients of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Science" title="National Medal of Science">National Medal of Science</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>2 recipients of the <a href="/wiki/National_Medal_of_Technology" title="National Medal of Technology" class="mw-redirect">National Medal of Technology</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>3 recipients of the <a href="/wiki/National_Humanities_Medal" title="National Humanities Medal">National Humanities Medal</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>51 members of <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>56 fellows of the <a href="/wiki/American_Physics_Society" title="American Physics Society" class="mw-redirect">American Physics Society</a> (since 1995);<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>4 <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>24 <a href="/wiki/MacArthur_Fellow" title="MacArthur Fellow" class="mw-redirect">MacArthur Fellows</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>7 <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Foundation_Prize" title="Wolf Foundation Prize" class="mw-redirect">Wolf Foundation Prize</a> winners;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>6 <a href="/wiki/Koret_Foundation" title="Koret Foundation">Koret Foundation</a> Prize winners;<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>2 <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Computational_Linguistics" title="Association for Computational Linguistics">ACL</a> Lifetime Achievement Award winners;<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>14 <a href="/wiki/AAAI" title="AAAI" class="mw-redirect">AAAI</a> fellows;<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>3 <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> winners.<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Teller_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Teller-105"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Stanford's faculty and former faculty includes 29 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">Nobel laureates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-StanfordFactsFaculty_4-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordFactsFaculty-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as 19 recipients (22 if visiting professors and consulting professors included) of the <a href="/wiki/Turing_Award" title="Turing Award">Turing Award</a>, the so-called &quot;Nobel Prize in computer science&quot;, comprising one third of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Stanford_University_people#Computer_science" title="List of Stanford University people">awards given</a> in its 44-year history. The university has 27 ACM fellows. It is also affiliated with 4 <a href="/wiki/G%C3%B6del_Prize" title="G&ouml;del Prize">G&ouml;del Prize</a> winners, 4 <a href="/wiki/Knuth_Prize" title="Knuth Prize">Knuth Prize</a> recipients, 10 <a href="/wiki/IJCAI_Computers_and_Thought_Award" title="IJCAI Computers and Thought Award">IJCAI Computers and Thought Award</a> winners, and about 15 <a href="/wiki/Grace_Murray_Hopper_Award" title="Grace Murray Hopper Award">Grace Murray Hopper Award</a> winners for their work in the foundations of computer science.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student">Student</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Student">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of 2011, 107 Stanford students or alumni have become <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" title="Rhodes Scholars" class="mw-redirect">Rhodes Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_centers_and_institutes">Research centers and institutes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Research centers and institutes">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG/220px-Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG/330px-Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG/440px-Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hoover_Tower_from_Main_Quad.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View of Hoover Tower from Main Quad.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Stanford Office of the Vice Provost and Dean of Research oversees more than eighteen <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://doresearch.stanford.edu/research-scholarship/interdisciplinary-laboratories-centers-and-institutes">Independent Laboratories, Centers, and Institutes</a> with a wide range of scholarly activities.</p> 
     <p>Other Stanford-affiliated institutions include the <a href="/wiki/SLAC_National_Accelerator_Laboratory" title="SLAC National Accelerator Laboratory">SLAC National Accelerator Laboratory</a> (originally the Stanford Linear Accelerator Center) and the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Research_Institute" title="Stanford Research Institute" class="mw-redirect">Stanford Research Institute</a>, a now independent institution which originated at the university, in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Humanities_Center" title="Stanford Humanities Center" class="mw-redirect">Stanford Humanities Center</a>.</p> 
     <p>Stanford also houses the <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Institution" title="Hoover Institution">Hoover Institution on War, Revolution and Peace</a>, a major <a href="/wiki/Policy" title="Policy">public policy</a> <a href="/wiki/Think_tank" title="Think tank">think tank</a> that attracts visiting scholars from around the world, and the <a href="/wiki/Freeman_Spogli_Institute_for_International_Studies" title="Freeman Spogli Institute for International Studies" class="mw-redirect">Freeman Spogli Institute for International Studies</a>, which is dedicated to the more specific study of <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>. Unable to locate a copy in any of its libraries, the Soviet Union was obliged to ask the Hoover Institution for a microfilm copy of its original edition of the first issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Pravda" title="Pravda">Pravda</a></i> (dated March 5, 1917).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Stanford is home to the <a href="/wiki/John_S._Knight_Fellowships_for_Professional_Journalists" title="John S. Knight Fellowships for Professional Journalists">John S. Knight Fellowships for Professional Journalist</a> and the Center for Ocean Solutions, which brings together marine science and policy to develop solutions to challenges facing the ocean. It also houses the <a href="/wiki/Hasso_Plattner_Institute_of_Design" title="Hasso Plattner Institute of Design">Hasso Plattner Institute of Design</a> (the &quot;d.school&quot;), a multidisciplinary design school in cooperation with the <a href="/wiki/Hasso_Plattner_Institute" title="Hasso Plattner Institute">Hasso Plattner Institute</a> of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Potsdam" title="University of Potsdam">University of Potsdam</a> that integrates product design, engineering, and business management education.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries_and_digital_resources">Libraries and digital resources</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Libraries and digital resources">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg/220px-Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg/330px-Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg/440px-Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_University_Green_Library_Bing_Wing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Green_Library" title="Green Library" class="mw-redirect">Green Library</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University_Libraries" title="Stanford University Libraries">Stanford University Libraries</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Stanford University Libraries and Academic Information Resources (SULAIR) hold a collection of nearly 9 million volumes, 260,000 rare or special books, 1.5 million e-books, 1.5 million audiovisual materials, 75,000 serials, 6 million microform holdings, and thousands of other digital resources, making it one of the largest and most diverse academic library systems in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-SULAIR_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SULAIR-108"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The main library in the SU library system is <a href="/wiki/Green_Library" title="Green Library" class="mw-redirect">Green Library</a>, which also contains various meeting and conference rooms, study spaces, and reading rooms. <a href="/wiki/Meyer_Library" title="Meyer Library" class="mw-redirect">Meyer Library</a>, a 24-hour library slated for demolition in 2015, holds various student-accessible media resources and houses one of the largest <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> collections, whose 540,000 volumes are being transported to an interim location while a new library is rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation_and_rankings">Reputation and rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Reputation and rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

        <td>2</td>

     </table> 
     <p>Stanford has been highly ranked by many international university rankings. It is second in the league table of the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> (<i>ARWU</i>) in 2012, and has been continuously considered the second or the third since 2003 when the first ARWU was released.<sup id="cite_ref-ARWU_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARWU-117"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, it ranked 15th in the <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>, which is collaborating with <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> to release its annual global ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i>(<i>THE</i>) of the same academic year considered it to be second, tied with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> while its <i><a href="/wiki/World_Reputation_Rankings" title="World Reputation Rankings" class="mw-redirect">World Reputation Rankings</a></i>, which is based on a survey of academics around the world and is a spin-off of the main world rankings, ranked it the sixth.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University's undergraduate program is ranked 6th among national universities by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> third by both <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Monthly" title="The Washington Monthly" class="mw-redirect">The Washington Monthly</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In the MINE ParisTech rankings in 2008 measuring the number of Chief Executive Officers among the Fortune Global 500, Stanford is ranked third in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011 Stanford was ranked second in the world according to the <a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i>, Stanford has produced the second highest number of billionaires of all universities, behind Harvard.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>From a 2010 poll done by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a></i>, Stanford is the most commonly named &quot;dream college&quot;, both for students and for parents, a title it has held in previous years.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> A 2003 <a href="/wiki/The_Gallup_Organization" title="The Gallup Organization" class="mw-redirect">Gallup</a> poll, which asked about the best colleges in the U.S., found that Stanford is the second-most prestigious university (behind Harvard) in the eyes of the general American public and roughly equal in prestige to Harvard among college-educated people.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div style="margin-left:0px">

             <td>1</td>

          </table> <p>In the 2012 <i>U.S. News Best Graduate Schools</i> rankings, Stanford was also placed in the top 5 for every discipline in which it was ranked, except industrial engineering, where it placed 6th, and fine arts where it placed 36th. Specifically, Stanford was ranked 1st in Business, 4th in Education, 2nd in Engineering, 2nd in Medicine, 2nd in Law, 1st in Biological Sciences, 4th in Chemistry, 1st in Computer Science, 4th in Earth Sciences, 2nd in Mathematics, 1st in Physics, 1st in Statistics, 5th in Economics, 2nd in English, 1st in History, 1st in Political Science, 1st in Psychology, 5th in Sociology. Within engineering, Stanford placed 1st in aerospace, computer, electrical, environmental, and mechanical engineering; 3rd in civil engineering; and 5th in chemical, material, and bioengineering.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> <p>In 2011-12, for the first time THE ranked Stanford 1st in the world for both humanities and social sciences, remarking &quot;Stanford University knocks Harvard University off the top spot in the arts and humanities subject rankings. With Pulitzer prizewinners and MacArthur Fellows leading its liberal-arts programme, the relative newcomer (founded in 1891) has proved more than a match for its illustrious Ivy League rival.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> </td> 
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Arts">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg/220px-Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg/330px-Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg/440px-Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Les-bourgeois-de-Calais.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Bronze statues by 
        <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Auguste Rodin</a> are scattered through the campus, including these 
        <i><a href="/wiki/The_Burghers_of_Calais" title="The Burghers of Calais">Burghers of Calais</a></i>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Stanford University is home to the <a href="/wiki/Iris_%26_B._Gerald_Cantor_Center_for_Visual_Arts" title="Iris &amp; B. Gerald Cantor Center for Visual Arts">Cantor Center for Visual Arts</a> museum with 24 galleries, sculpture gardens, terraces, and a courtyard first established in 1891 by Jane and Leland Stanford as a memorial to their only child. Notably, the Center possesses the largest collection of Rodin works outside of Paris, France. The <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Welton_Stanford" title="Thomas Welton Stanford">Thomas Welton Stanford</a> Gallery, built in 1917, serves as a teaching resource for the Department of Art &amp; Art History as well as an exhibition venue. There are also a large number of outdoor art installations throughout the campus, primarily sculptures, but some murals as well. The Papua New Guinea Sculpture Garden near Roble Hall features handmade wood carvings and &quot;totem poles.&quot;</p> 
     <p>Stanford has a thriving artistic and musical community. Extracurricular activities include theater groups such as Ram's Head Theatrical Society and the Stanford Shakespeare Society, award-winning <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> music groups such as the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Mendicants" title="Stanford Mendicants">Mendicants</a>, Counterpoint, the Stanford Fleet Street Singers, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Harmonics" title="Stanford Harmonics">Harmonics</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_Mixed_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stanford Mixed Company (page does not exist)">Mixed Company</a>, Testimony, <a href="/wiki/Talisman_A_Cappella" title="Talisman A Cappella" class="mw-redirect">Talisman</a>, Everyday People, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Raagapella" title="Stanford Raagapella">Raagapella</a>, and a group dedicated to performing the works of <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_and_Sullivan" title="Gilbert and Sullivan">Gilbert and Sullivan</a>, the Stanford Savoyards. Beyond these, the music department sponsors many ensembles including five choirs, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_Symphony_Orchestra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stanford Symphony Orchestra (page does not exist)">Stanford Symphony Orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Taiko" title="Stanford Taiko">Stanford Taiko</a>, and the Stanford Wind Ensemble.</p> 
     <p>Stanford's dance community is one of the most vibrant in the country, with an active dance division in the Drama Department and over 30 different dance-related student groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Band" title="Stanford Band">Stanford Band</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Band#The_Dollies" title="Stanford Band">Dollie</a> dance troupe.</p> 
     <p>Perhaps most distinctive of all is its <a href="/wiki/Social_dance" title="Social dance">social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vintage_dance" title="Vintage dance">vintage dance</a> community, cultivated by dance historian <a href="/wiki/Richard_Powers_(dance_historian)" title="Richard Powers (dance historian)">Richard Powers</a> and enjoyed by hundreds of students and thousands of alumni. Stanford hosts monthly informal dances (called Jammix) and large quarterly dance events, including Ragtime Ball (fall), the Stanford Viennese Ball (winter), and Big Dance (spring). Stanford also boasts a student-run swing performance troupe called <a href="/wiki/Swingtime_Dance_Troupe" title="Swingtime Dance Troupe">Swingtime</a> and several alumni performance groups, including Decadance and the Academy of Danse Libre.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Creative_writing" title="Creative writing">creative writing</a> program brings young writers to campus via the <a href="/wiki/Stegner_Fellowship" title="Stegner Fellowship">Stegner Fellowships</a> and other graduate scholarship programs. <i><a href="/wiki/This_Boy%27s_Life" title="This Boy's Life">This Boy's Life</a></i> author <a href="/wiki/Tobias_Wolff" title="Tobias Wolff">Tobias Wolff</a> teaches writing to undergraduates and graduate students. Knight Journalism Fellows are invited to spend a year at the campus taking seminars and courses of their choice. There is also an extracurricular writing and performance group called the Stanford Spoken Word Collective, which also serves as the school's poetry slam team.</p> 
     <p>Stanford also hosts various publishing courses for professionals. Stanford Professional Publishing Course, which was offered on campus since the late 1970s, brought together international publishing professionals to discuss changing business models in magazine and book publishing. It ended in 2009, although the tradition has continued at Yale with the Yale Publishing Course that began in 2010. Videos from the Stanford Professional Publishing Courses are still made available on their website.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford-bikes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Stanford-bikes.jpg/220px-Stanford-bikes.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Stanford-bikes.jpg/330px-Stanford-bikes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Stanford-bikes.jpg/440px-Stanford-bikes.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford-bikes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Many students use bicycles to get around the large campus.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div>
