     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg/220px-Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg/330px-Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg/440px-Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_University_campus_from_above.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> View from 
        <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Tower" title="Hoover Tower">Hoover Tower</a> observation deck of the Quad and surrounding area, facing west
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Stanford enrolled 7,063 undergraduate<sup id="cite_ref-gradinfo_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradinfo-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> and 11,154 graduate students<sup id="cite_ref-gradinfo_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradinfo-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> in the 2012?2013 year. Women comprised 48% of undergraduates and 41% of professional and graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The freshman retention rate for 2010 was 98%, the four-year graduation rate is 78.4%, and the six-year rate is 95%.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The relatively low four-year graduation rate is a function of the university's coterminal degree (or &quot;coterm&quot;) program, which allows students to earn a Master's degree as an extension of their undergraduate program.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Stanford awarded 1,715 undergraduate degrees, 2,278 Master's degrees, 764 doctoral degrees, and 366 professional degrees in the 2011-2012 school year.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> The most popular Bachelor's degrees were in the social sciences, interdisciplinary studies, and engineering.</p> 
     <p>For the class of 2016, Stanford received 36,631 applications and accepted 2427 or 6.6%, the lowest in the university's history and the second lowest in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The cost of attendance in 2010?2011 is $54,947.<sup id="cite_ref-gradinfo_137-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradinfo-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford's admission process is need-blind for US citizens and permanent residents; while it is not need-blind for international students, 64% are on need-based aid, with an average aid package of $31,411.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, the university awarded $117 million in financial aid to 3,530 students, with an average aid package of $40,593.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> Total external and internal aid (including jobs and optional loans) amounted to $172.3 million to undergraduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-gradinfo_137-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradinfo-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Eighty percent of students are on some form of financial aid.<sup id="cite_ref-gradinfo_137-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradinfo-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford's no-loan policy waives tuition, room, and board for families with incomes below $60,000, and families with incomes below $100,000 are not required to pay tuition (those with incomes up to $150,000 will have tuition significantly reduced).<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> 17% of students receive Pell Grants,<sup id="cite_ref-gradinfo_137-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gradinfo-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> a common measure of low-income students at a college. Fifteen percent of the undergraduates are first-generation students.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dormitories_and_student_housing">Dormitories and student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Dormitories and student housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Eighty-nine percent of undergraduate students live in on-campus university housing. First-year students are required to live on campus, and all undergraduates are guaranteed housing for all four undergraduate years.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_98-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the Stanford Housing Assignments Office, undergraduates live in 80 different houses, including dormitories, co-ops, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Row_House_Program" title="Stanford Row House Program">row houses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University#Greek_life" title="Stanford University">fraternities and sororities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ugradres_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ugradres-147"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> At Manzanita Park, 118 <a href="/wiki/Mobile_home" title="Mobile home">mobile homes</a> were installed as &quot;temporary&quot; housing from 1969 to 1991, but it is now the site of modern dorms Castano, Kimball, and Lantana.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Most student residences are located just outside the campus core, within ten minutes (on foot or bike) of most classrooms and libraries. Some are for freshmen only; others give priority to sophomores, others to both freshmen and sophomores; some are for upperclass students only, and some are open to all four classes. Most residences are co-ed; seven are all-male <a href="/wiki/Fraternity" title="Fraternity">fraternities</a>, three are all-female <a href="/wiki/Sorority" title="Sorority" class="mw-redirect">sororities</a>, and there is also one all-female non-sorority house, Roth House. In most residences, men and women live on the same floor, but a few dorms are configured for men and women to live on separate floors (single-gender floors), including all Wilbur dorms except for Arroyo and Okada.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Beginning in 2009?10, the University's housing plan anticipates that all freshmen desiring to live in all-freshman dorms will be accommodated. In the 2009?10 year, almost two-thirds of freshmen will be housed in Stern and Wilbur Halls. The one-third who requested four-class housing will be located in other dormitories throughout campus, including Florence Moore (FloMo).<sup id="cite_ref-froshhousing_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-froshhousing-150"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 2008, Stanford unveiled a new pilot plan to test out gender-neutral housing in five campus residences, allowing males and females to live in the same room. This was after concerted student pressure, as well as the institution of similar policies at peer institutions such as <a href="/wiki/Wesleyan_University" title="Wesleyan University">Wesleyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oberlin_College" title="Oberlin College">Oberlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clark_University" title="Clark University">Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dartmouth_College" title="Dartmouth College">Dartmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">UPenn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-genderblind_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genderblind-151"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Several residences are considered theme houses. The Academic, Language and Culture Houses include EAST (Education And Society Theme), Hammarskj&ouml;ld (International Theme), Haus Mitteleuropa (Central European Theme), La Casa Italiana (Italian Language and Culture), La Maison Fran&ccedil;aise (French Language and Culture House), Slavianskii Dom (Slavic/East European Theme House), Storey (Human Biology Theme House), and Yost (Spanish Language and Culture).Cross-Cultural Theme Houses include Casa Zapata (Chicano/Latino Theme in Stern Hall), Muwekma-tah-ruk (American Indian/Alaska Native, and Native Hawaiian Theme), Okada (Asian-American Theme in Wilbur Hall), and Ujamaa (Black/African-American Theme in Lagunita Court). Focus Houses include Freshman-Sophomore College (Freshman Focus), Branner Hall (Community Service), Kimball (Arts &amp; Performing Arts), Crothers (Global Citizenship), and Toyon (Sophomore Priority).<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Theme houses predating the current &quot;theme&quot; classification system are Columbae (Social Change Through Nonviolence, since 1970),<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> and Synergy (Exploring Alternatives, since 1972).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Another famous style of housing at Stanford is the <a href="/wiki/Housing_cooperative" title="Housing cooperative">co-ops</a>. These houses feature cooperative living, where residents and eating associates each contribute work to keep the house running, such as cooking meals or cleaning shared spaces. The co-ops on campus are Chi Theta Chi, Columbae, Enchanted Broccoli Forest (EBF), Hammarskj&ouml;ld (which is also the International Theme House), Kairos, Terra, and Synergy.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>At any time, around 50 percent of the graduate population lives on campus. Now that construction has concluded on the new Munger graduate residence, this percentage has probably increased. First-year graduate students are guaranteed housing.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_banner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Stanford_banner.jpg/220px-Stanford_banner.jpg" width="220" height="345" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Stanford_banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/db/Stanford_banner.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stanford_banner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Vintage Stanford University postcard
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Uncommon Man/Uncommon Woman: Stanford does not award honorary degrees,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> but in 1953 the University created the degree of Uncommon Man/Uncommon Woman for individuals who give rare and extraordinary service to the University. The University's highest honor, the degree is not given at prescribed intervals, but only when appropriate to recognize extraordinary service. Recipients include <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Hewlett" title="Bill Hewlett" class="mw-redirect">Bill Hewlett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dave_Packard" title="Dave Packard" class="mw-redirect">Dave Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lucile_Packard_Foundation_for_Children%27s_Health#Lucile_Packard" title="Lucile Packard Foundation for Children's Health">Lucile Packard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_W._Gardner" title="John W. Gardner">John Gardner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Big_Game_(football)" title="Big Game (football)" class="mw-redirect">Big Game</a> events: The events in the week leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Big_Game_(football)" title="Big Game (football)" class="mw-redirect">Big Game</a> vs. <a href="/wiki/California_Golden_Bears_football" title="California Golden Bears football">UC Berkeley</a>, including Gaieties (a musical written, composed, produced, and performed by the students of Ram's Head Theatrical Society), The Bearial (in which the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Band" title="Stanford Band">Stanford Band</a> performs a funeral-like procession and pierces a stuffed-animal bear on the tip of the Stanford Claw fountain), and an hourly train whistle that counts down the hours until Big Game, orchestrated by the Stanford Axe Committee.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
      <li>Viennese Ball: a formal <a href="/wiki/Ball_(dance)" title="Ball (dance)">ball</a> with <a href="/wiki/Waltzes" title="Waltzes" class="mw-redirect">waltzes</a> that was initially started in the 1970s by students returning from the now-closed Stanford in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> overseas program.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> It is now open to all students.</li> 
      <li>Mausoleum Party: An annual <a href="/wiki/Halloween" title="Halloween">Halloween</a> Party at the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Mausoleum" title="Stanford Mausoleum">Stanford Mausoleum</a>, which contains the corpses of <a href="/wiki/Leland_Stanford,_Jr." title="Leland Stanford, Jr.">Leland Stanford, Jr.</a> and his parents. A 20-year tradition, the Mausoleum party was on hiatus from 2002 to 2005<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> due to a lack of funding from the alumni,<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> but was revived in 2006. In 2008, it was hosted in Old Union rather than at the actual Mausoleum, because rain prohibited generators from being rented.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, after fundraising efforts by the Junior Class Presidents and the ASSU Executive, the event was able to return to the Mausoleum despite facing budget cuts earlier in the year.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/The_Game_(treasure_hunt)" title="The Game (treasure hunt)">The Game</a>: The Game is a treasure hunt put on by dorm staff usually in the spring and summer quarters.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>Former campus traditions include the Big Game bonfire on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Lagunita" title="Lake Lagunita">Lake Lagunita</a> (a seasonal lake usually dry in the fall), which is now inactive because of the presence of endangered salamanders in the lake bed.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Fraternities and sororities have been active on the Stanford campus since 1891, when the University first opened. In 1944, University President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Tresidder" title="Donald Tresidder">Donald Tresidder</a> banned all Stanford sororities due to extreme competition.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> However, following <a href="/wiki/Title_IX" title="Title IX">Title IX</a>, the Board of Trustees lifted the 33-year ban on sororities in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford is now home to 29 Greek organizations, including 13 sororities and 16 fraternities, representing 13% of undergraduates. In contrast to many universities, nine of the ten housed Greek organizations live in University-owned houses, the exception being <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, which owns its own house (but not the land) on The Row. Six chapters are members of the African American Fraternal and Sororal Association, 11 chapters are members of the Interfraternity Council, 6 chapters belong to the Intersorority Council, and 6 chapters belong to the Multicultural Greek Council.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Stanford is home to three unhoused historically NPHC (<a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a> or &quot;Divine Nine&quot;) three sororities (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Alpha" title="Alpha Kappa Alpha">Alpha Kappa Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Theta" title="Delta Sigma Theta">Delta Sigma Theta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Gamma_Rho" title="Sigma Gamma Rho">Sigma Gamma Rho</a>) and three unhoused NPHC fraternities (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">Alpha Phi Alpha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Psi" title="Kappa Alpha Psi">Kappa Alpha Psi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Phi_Beta_Sigma" title="Phi Beta Sigma">Phi Beta Sigma</a>). These fraternities and sororities operate under the AAFSA (African American Fraternal Sororal Association) at Stanford.</li> 
      <li>Seven historically NPC (<a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a>) sororities, four of which are unhoused (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Phi" title="Alpha Epsilon Phi">Alpha Epsilon Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chi_Omega" title="Chi Omega">Chi Omega</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>) and three of which are housed (<a href="/wiki/Delta_Delta_Delta" title="Delta Delta Delta">Delta Delta Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a>) call Stanford home. These sororities operate under the Stanford Inter-sorority Council (ISC).</li> 
      <li>Eleven historically NIC (<a href="/wiki/National_Interfraternity_Conference" title="National Interfraternity Conference" class="mw-redirect">National Interfraternity Conference</a>) fraternities are also represented at Stanford, including four unhoused fraternities (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Delta Kappa Epsilon">Delta Kappa Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Tau_Delta" title="Delta Tau Delta">Delta Tau Delta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Epsilon" title="Sigma Phi Epsilon">Sigma Phi Epsilon</a>), and seven housed fraternities (<a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Order" title="Kappa Alpha Order">Kappa Alpha Order</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Sigma" title="Kappa Sigma">Kappa Sigma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Epsilon" title="Sigma Alpha Epsilon">Sigma Alpha Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Nu" title="Sigma Nu">Sigma Nu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Theta_Delta_Chi" title="Theta Delta Chi">Theta Delta Chi</a>). These fraternities operate under the Stanford Inter-fraternity Council (IFC).</li> 
      <li>There are also four unhoused MGC (Multicultural Greek Council) sororities on campus (<a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Kappa Delta Phi">Alpha Kappa Delta Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Theta_Nu" title="Lambda Theta Nu">Lambda Theta Nu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Psi_Zeta" title="Sigma Psi Zeta">Sigma Psi Zeta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Theta_Psi" title="Sigma Theta Psi">Sigma Theta Psi</a>), as well as two unhoused MGC fraternities (<a href="/wiki/Gamma_Zeta_Alpha" title="Gamma Zeta Alpha">Gamma Zeta Alpha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Phi_Epsilon" title="Lambda Phi Epsilon">Lambda Phi Epsilon</a>). Lambda Phi Epsilon is recognized by the National Interfraternity Conference (NIC).<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_groups">Student groups</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Student groups">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Stanford offers its students the opportunity to engage in over 650 groups.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> Groups are often, though not always, partially funded by the University via allocations directed by the student government organization, the ASSU. These funds include &quot;special fees&quot;, which are decided by a Spring Quarter vote by the student body. Groups span from Athletic/Recreational, Careers/Pre-professional, Community Service, Ethnic/Cultural, Fraternities/Sororities, Health/Counseling, Media/Publications, Music/Dance/Creative Arts, Political/Social Awareness to Religious/Philosophical.</p> 
     <p>Groups include (but are not limited to):</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Stanford_Daily" title="Stanford Daily" class="mw-redirect">Stanford Daily</a></i> is an independent organization located on campus, and is the daily newspaper serving Stanford University. It has been published since the University was founded in 1892.</li> 
      <li>The Stanford Axe Committee is the official guardian of the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Axe" title="Stanford Axe">Stanford Axe</a> and the rest of the time assists the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Band" title="Stanford Band">Stanford Band</a> as a supplementary spirit group.</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=SUpost.com&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SUpost.com (page does not exist)">SUpost.com</a></i> is an online marketplace for Stanford students and alumni, in partnership with Stanford Student Enterprises (SSE).<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Stanford Pre-Business Association<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> is the largest business-focused undergraduate organization. It plays an instrumental role in establishing an active link between the industry, alumni, and student communities.</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/wiki/Stanford_solar_car_project" title="Stanford solar car project" class="mw-redirect">Stanford solar car project</a>, where students build a solar-powered car every 2 years and race it in either the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Solar_Challenge" title="North American Solar Challenge">North American Solar Challenge</a> or the <a href="/wiki/World_Solar_Challenge" title="World Solar Challenge">World Solar Challenge</a>.</li> 
      <li>Stanford Astronomical Society organizes viewings of meteor showers, lunar eclipses, and other astronomical events.</li> 
      <li>The Stanford Kite Flying Society<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> (founded 2008), a group of undergraduates dedicated to flying kites. Society &quot;meetings&quot; are usually on Wilbur Field when it is windy out.</li> 
      <li>The Pilipino American Student Union (PASU),<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> a culture-oriented community service and social activism group. Also integral to PASU is a traditional performing arts arm called Kayumanggi.</li> 
      <li>Stanford Finance is a pre-professional organization aimed at mentoring students who want to enter a career in finance, through mentors and internships.</li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leland_Quarterly&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leland Quarterly (page does not exist)">Leland Quarterly</a><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> is Stanford's literary magazine. It publishes the creative writing, essays, and art of Stanford students on a &quot;Stanford quarterly&quot; basis (autumn, winter, and spring) and also runs features of arts and literary figures and events on campus.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/KZSU" title="KZSU">KZSU</a> Stanford 90.1 FM is the student-run radio station which features freeform music programming, sports commentary, and news segments.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Business_Association_of_Stanford_Entrepreneurial_Students" title="Business Association of Stanford Entrepreneurial Students">BASES</a>, the Business Association of Stanford Entrepreneurial Students is one of the largest professional organizations in Silicon Valley, with over 5,000 members. Its goal is to support the next generation of entrepreneurs.</li> 
      <li>The Stanford Robber Barons are Stanford's only sketch comedy group, and perform original material for free every quarter on campus. They regularly host events, and have performed at the <a href="/wiki/Laugh_Factory" title="Laugh Factory">Laugh Factory</a> and at the <a href="/wiki/SF_SketchFest" title="SF SketchFest" class="mw-redirect">SF SketchFest</a>.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">A cappella</a> groups include the Mendicants (all male),<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> the Stanford Fleet Street Singers (all male),<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> Counterpoint (all female),<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Raagapella" title="Stanford Raagapella">Stanford Raagapella</a><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> and Mixed Company (coed).<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> Because Fleet Street maintains Stanford songs as a regular part of its performing repertoire, Stanford University used the group as ambassadors during the University's centennial celebration and commissioned an album, entitled <i>Up Toward Mountains Higher</i> (1999), of Stanford songs which were sent to alumni around the world.</li> 
      <li>The Stanford Martial Arts Program (SMAP) is an umbrella organization for 11 different martial arts groups on campus: Aikido, Capoeira, Eskrima, Judo, Jujitsu, Kenpo Karate, Muay Thai, Wing Chun, JKA Shotokan, Taekwondo, and Wushu.</li> 
      <li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_Women_In_Business&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Stanford Women In Business (page does not exist)">Stanford Women In Business</a> (SWIB)<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> is an on-campus business organization consisting of over a board of 40 and 100 active members. Each year, SWIB organizes over 25 events and workshops, hosts a winter and spring conference, and provides mentorship and spring quarter internships.</li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Claw_Magazine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Claw Magazine (page does not exist)">The Claw Magazine</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> named after <a href="/wiki/Mem_Claw" title="Mem Claw" class="mw-redirect">the fountain in White Plaza</a>, is an undergraduate publication that features humor, artwork, investigative reporting, and fiction.</li> 
      <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Free_Stanford_forum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Free Stanford forum (page does not exist)">Free Stanford forum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> Everything about life at Stanford University. Campus, careers, education, visa, faq and more. Interesting insights at Stanford University.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Chi_Alpha_Christian_Fellowship" title="Chi Alpha Christian Fellowship" class="mw-redirect">Chi Alpha Christian Fellowship</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> A Christian organization at Stanford University meeting weekly on Wednesday nights at 7:30 pm in room 370-370.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/StartX" title="StartX">StartX</a> is a non-profilt startup accelerator for student and faculty-led <a href="/wiki/Startup_company" title="Startup company">startups</a><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> that over 12% of the study body has applied to. It is staffed primarily by students.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Cardinal" title="Stanford Cardinal">Stanford Cardinal</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Stanford participates in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA's</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> <a href="/wiki/Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="Football Bowl Subdivision" class="mw-redirect">FBS</a> and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>. It also participates in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a> for indoor <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track</a> (men and women), fencing (men and women), <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a> (men and women), <a href="/wiki/Artistic_gymnastics" title="Artistic gymnastics">gymnastics</a> (men and women), <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_lacrosse" title="Women's lacrosse">women's lacrosse</a>, and men's <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>. The women's <a href="/wiki/Field_hockey" title="Field hockey">field hockey</a> team is part of the <a href="/wiki/NorPac_Conference" title="NorPac Conference" class="mw-redirect">NorPac Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford's traditional sports rival is the <a href="/wiki/California_Golden_Bears" title="California Golden Bears">University of California, Berkeley</a>, its neighbor to the north in the East Bay.</p> 
     <p>Stanford has had at least one NCAA team champion every year since the 1976-77 school year<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> and has earned 104 NCAA national team titles<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> since its establishment, second most behind the <a href="/wiki/UCLA_Bruins" title="UCLA Bruins">University of California, Los Angeles</a>, and 467 individual National championships, the most by any university.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford has won the award for the top-ranked collegiate athletic program?the <a href="/wiki/NACDA_Director%27s_Cup" title="NACDA Director's Cup" class="mw-redirect">NACDA Director's Cup</a>, formerly known as the Sears Cup?every year for the past seventeen years.</p> 
     <p>Stanford offers 36 varsity sports (18 female, 15 male, one coed), 19 club sports and 37 intramural sports?about 800 students participate in intercollegiate sports. The university offers about 300 athletic scholarships.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Stanstadium_view.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Stanstadium_view.jpg/220px-Stanstadium_view.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Stanstadium_view.jpg/330px-Stanstadium_view.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Stanstadium_view.jpg/440px-Stanstadium_view.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Stanstadium_view.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The new 
        <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Stadium" title="Stanford Stadium">Stanford Stadium</a>, site of home football games.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The winner of the annual &quot;<a href="/wiki/Big_Game_(football)" title="Big Game (football)" class="mw-redirect">Big Game</a>&quot; between the <a href="/wiki/California_Golden_Bears_football" title="California Golden Bears football">Cal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Cardinal_football" title="Stanford Cardinal football">Stanford</a> football teams gains custody of <a href="/wiki/The_Stanford_Axe" title="The Stanford Axe" class="mw-redirect">the Stanford Axe</a>. The first &quot;Big Game&quot;, played at Haight Street Park in San Francisco on March 19, 1892, established football on the west coast. Stanford won 14 to 10 in front of 8 thousand spectators. Stanford's football team played in the first <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_(game)" title="Rose Bowl (game)" class="mw-redirect">Rose Bowl</a> in 1902. However, the violence of the sport at the time, coupled with the post-game rioting of drunken spectators, led San Francisco to bar further &quot;Big Games&quot; in the city in 1905. In 1906, David Starr Jordan banned football from Stanford. The 1906?1914 &quot;Big Game&quot; contests featured rugby instead of football. Stanford football was resumed in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-Starr3_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Starr3-188"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford won back-to-back Rose Bowls in 1971 and 1972. Stanford has played in 13 Rose Bowls, most recently in 2013. Stanford's <a href="/wiki/Jim_Plunkett" title="Jim Plunkett">Jim Plunkett</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Heisman_Trophy" title="Heisman Trophy">Heisman Trophy</a> in 1970.</p> 
     <p>Club sports, while not officially a part of Stanford athletics, are numerous at Stanford. Sports include <a href="/wiki/Archery" title="Archery">archery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">badminton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">cheerleading</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">cycling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurling" title="Hurling">hurling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kayaking" title="Kayaking">kayaking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">men's lacrosse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racquetball" title="Racquetball">racquetball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_(sport)" title="Ultimate (sport)">Ultimate</a>. The men's Ultimate team won national championships in 1984 and 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-UPA_College_Open_Champions_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPA_College_Open_Champions-189"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> the women's Ultimate team in 1997, 1998, 1999, 2003, 2005, 2006, and 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-UPA_College_Women.27s_Champions_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UPA_College_Women.27s_Champions-190"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> the women's rugby team in 1999, 2005, 2006 and 2008. The cycling team won the 2007 Division I USA Cycling Collegiate Road National Championships.</p> 
     <p>Until 1930, Stanford did not have a &quot;mascot&quot; name for its athletic teams. In that year, the athletic department adopted the name &quot;Indians.&quot; In 1972, &quot;Indians&quot; was dropped after a complaint of racial insensitivity was lodged by Native American students.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg/220px-11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg/330px-11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg/440px-11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:11-04-06-LSJUMB-003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Leland_Stanford_Junior_University_Marching_Band" title="Leland Stanford Junior University Marching Band" class="mw-redirect">Leland Stanford Junior University Marching Band</a> rallies football fans with arrangements of &quot;All Right Now&quot; and other contemporary music.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Stanford sports teams are now officially referred to as the Stanford <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(color)" title="Cardinal (color)">Cardinal</a>, referring to the deep red color, not the <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(bird)" title="Cardinal (bird)">cardinal bird</a>. Stanford is unusual in that it has only had one official color, Cardinal red, not two colors like most colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-RKMLSJU_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RKMLSJU-191"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup> Since the 19th century. The Band's mascot, <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Tree" title="Stanford Tree">&quot;The Tree&quot;</a>, has become associated with the school in general. Part of the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Band" title="Stanford Band">Leland Stanford Junior University Marching Band (LSJUMB)</a>, the tree symbol derives from the <a href="/wiki/El_Palo_Alto" title="El Palo Alto">El Palo Alto</a> redwood tree on the Stanford and City of Palo Alto seals.</p> 
     <p>Stanford hosts an annual <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_Series" title="U.S. Open Series" class="mw-redirect">U.S. Open Series</a> tennis tournament, the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_West_Classic" title="Bank of the West Classic">Bank of the West Classic</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Taube_Stadium" title="Taube Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Taube Stadium</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cobb_Track&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cobb Track (page does not exist)">Cobb Track</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Angell_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Angell Field (page does not exist)">Angell Field</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Avery_Stadium_Pool&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Avery Stadium Pool (page does not exist)">Avery Stadium Pool</a> are considered world-class athletic facilities. <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Stadium" title="Stanford Stadium">Stanford Stadium</a> hosted <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XIX" title="Super Bowl XIX">Super Bowl XIX</a> on January 20, 1985, in which the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> by a score of 38?16, and several group stage matches in the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a>.</p> 
     <p>According to the <i>Stanford Daily</i>, &quot;Stanford has been represented in every summer Olympiad since 1908.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-olympics_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympics-192"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2004, Stanford athletes had won 182 Olympic medals at the summer games; &quot;in fact, in every Olympiad since 1912, Stanford athletes have won at least one and as many as 17 gold medals.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-olympicmedals_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympicmedals-193"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> Stanford athletes won 16 medals at the 2012 Summer Games?12 gold, 2 silver and 2 bronze.<sup id="cite_ref-olympics12_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympics12-194"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty">Notable faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Notable faculty">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of late 2012, Stanford has 1,995 tenure-line faculty, senior fellows, center fellows, and medical center faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Professors who have served in government include Former Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a>, Former Secretary of Defense <a href="/wiki/William_Perry" title="William Perry">William Perry</a>, Former US Ambassador to Afghanistan Lt. General <a href="/wiki/Karl_Eikenberry" title="Karl Eikenberry">Karl Eikenberry</a>, current US Ambassador to Russia <a href="/wiki/Michael_McFaul" title="Michael McFaul">Michael McFaul</a>, Former Chair of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Economic_Advisors" title="Council of Economic Advisors" class="mw-redirect">Council of Economic Advisors</a> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Lazear" title="Edward Lazear">Edward Lazear</a> and Former <a href="/wiki/Director_of_policy_planning" title="Director of policy planning" class="mw-redirect">director of policy planning</a> for the US State Dept. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_D._Krasner" title="Stephen D. Krasner">Stephen D. Krasner</a>. <a href="/wiki/George_Schultz" title="George Schultz" class="mw-redirect">George Schultz</a>, Former Secretary of State, Secretary of Labor and Secretary of the Treasury, is a fellow at the <a href="/wiki/Hoover_Institution" title="Hoover Institution">Hoover Institution</a> and lectures at the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Graduate_School_of_Business" title="Stanford Graduate School of Business">Stanford Graduate School of Business</a>. Former President of Peru <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Toledo" title="Alejandro Toledo">Alejandro Toledo</a> was a distinguished lecturer from 2007-2009.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Siegfried_Hecker" title="Siegfried Hecker">Siegfried Hecker</a>, director emeritus of <a href="/wiki/Los_Alamos_National_Laboratory" title="Los Alamos National Laboratory">Los Alamos National Laboratory</a>, makes frequent visits to North Korea to inspect their nuclear weapons facilities, and co-teaches a class on national security with William Perry. <a href="/wiki/Tenzin_Tethong" title="Tenzin Tethong">Tenzin Tethong</a>, former prime minister of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Tibetan_Administration" title="Central Tibetan Administration">Central Tibetan Administration</a>, chairs the university's Tibetan Studies Initiative, and was a candidate for Prime Minister of the Tibetan Government in Exile.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> Former US President <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Harrison" title="Benjamin Harrison">Benjamin Harrison</a> was a founding professor at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Law_School" title="Stanford Law School">Stanford Law School</a>.</p> 
     <p>The Freeman Spogli Institute for International Studies is also home to political theorist <a href="/wiki/Francis_Fukuyama" title="Francis Fukuyama">Francis Fukuyama</a>, and founding editor of the <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_Democracy" title="Journal of Democracy">Journal of Democracy</a> and advisor to the Coalition Provisional Authority in Iraq, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Diamond" title="Larry Diamond">Larry Diamond</a>.</p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanities_and_social_sciences">Humanities and social sciences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Humanities and social sciences">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Professor <a href="/wiki/Philip_Zimbardo" title="Philip Zimbardo">Philip Zimbardo</a> is a leading social psychologist, and oversaw the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Prison_Experiment" title="Stanford Prison Experiment" class="mw-redirect">Stanford Prison Experiment</a>, and psychologist <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Terman" title="Lewis Terman">Lewis Terman</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Stanford-Binet_IQ_Test" title="Stanford-Binet IQ Test" class="mw-redirect">Stanford-Binet IQ Test</a>. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Bandura" title="Albert Bandura">Albert Bandura</a> conducted the famed <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bobo_Doll_Experiment&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bobo Doll Experiment (page does not exist)">Bobo Doll Experiment</a>, contributing significantly to <a href="/wiki/Social_learning_theory" title="Social learning theory">social learning theory</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tobias_Wolff" title="Tobias Wolff">Tobias Wolff</a>, best known for his memoir <i><a href="/wiki/This_Boy%27s_Life" title="This Boy's Life">This Boy's Life</a></i>, is a member of the creative writing faculty. Philosophy Professor <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Cohen_(philosopher)" title="Joshua Cohen (philosopher)">Joshua Cohen</a> is a widely cited scholar in political science, philosophy, and ethics. History Professor <a href="/wiki/Jack_N._Rakove" title="Jack N. Rakove">Jack N. Rakove</a> won the Pulitzer Prize for his book on the history of the constitution, the subject of a course he teaches at Stanford.</p> 
     <p>In 2012, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nemerov" title="Alexander Nemerov">Alexander Nemerov</a>, prominent art historian and chair of the History of Art Department at <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, would join the Stanford faculty as part of the University's efforts to increase its presence in the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The economics department and the Hoover Institution have also been home to more than nine Nobel Prize winners in economics, including <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Arrow" title="Kenneth Arrow">Kenneth Arrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton_Friedman" title="Milton Friedman">Milton Friedman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Becker" title="Gary Becker">Gary Becker</a>. Chair of the economics department <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Levin_(economist)" title="Jonathan Levin (economist)">Jonathan Levin</a> won the 2011 <a href="/wiki/John_Bates_Clark_Medal" title="John Bates Clark Medal">John Bates Clark Medal</a>, awarded to the leading economist under 40. Economist <a href="/wiki/John_B._Taylor" title="John B. Taylor">John B. Taylor</a> served as the <a href="/wiki/Under_Secretary_of_the_Treasury" title="Under Secretary of the Treasury" class="mw-redirect">Under Secretary of the Treasury</a> for International affairs, and developed the <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Rule" title="Taylor Rule" class="mw-redirect">Taylor Rule</a>. Professor <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Hoxby" title="Caroline Hoxby">Caroline Hoxby</a> is a leading education economist and directs of the Economics of Education Program for the <a href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Economic_Research" title="National Bureau of Economic Research">National Bureau of Economic Research</a>. She is married to fellow Rhodes Scholar and Stanford English Professor Blair Hoxby.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni">Notable alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable alumni">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Stanford_University_people" title="List of Stanford University people">List of Stanford University people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Stanford alumni have started many companies, with Forbes magazine remarking, &quot;it is almost impossible to name a leading-edge company in Silicon Valley that isn't closely associated with Stanford.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StanfordAlumCompanies_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StanfordAlumCompanies-200"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> Companies founded by Stanford alumni include <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a> (<a href="/wiki/William_Reddington_Hewlett" title="William Reddington Hewlett" class="mw-redirect">William Hewlett</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Packard" title="David Packard">David Packard</a>), <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sandra_Lerner" title="Sandra Lerner">Sandra Lerner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Bosack" title="Leonard Bosack">Leonard Bosack</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">Nvidia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jen-Hsun_Huang" title="Jen-Hsun Huang">Jen-Hsun Huang</a>), <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">SGI</a>, <a href="/wiki/VMware" title="VMware">VMware</a>, <a href="/wiki/MIPS_Technologies" title="MIPS Technologies">MIPS Technologies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jerry_Yang_(entrepreneur)" title="Jerry Yang (entrepreneur)">Chih-Yuan Yang</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Filo" title="David Filo">David Filo</a>), <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Page" title="Lawrence Page" class="mw-redirect">Lawrence Page</a>), <a href="/wiki/Wipro_Technologies" title="Wipro Technologies" class="mw-redirect">Wipro Technologies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azim_Premji" title="Azim Premji">Azim Premji</a>), <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a> (<a href="/wiki/Phil_Knight" title="Phil Knight">Phil Knight</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gap_(clothing_retailer)" title="Gap (clothing retailer)" class="mw-redirect">Gap</a> (<a href="/wiki/Doris_F._Fisher" title="Doris F. Fisher">Doris F. Fisher</a>), <a href="/wiki/Palantir_Technologies" title="Palantir Technologies">Palantir Technologies</a> (<a href="/wiki/Joe_Lonsdale" title="Joe Lonsdale">Joe Lonsdale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Cohen_(entrepreneur)" title="Stephen Cohen (entrepreneur)">Stephen Cohen</a>), <a href="/wiki/Logitech" title="Logitech">Logitech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snapchat" title="Snapchat">Snapchat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vinod_Khosla" title="Vinod Khosla">Vinod Khosla</a>). The <i>Sun</i> in Sun Microsystems originally stood for &quot;Stanford University Network.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> Other companies and organizations founded or co-founded by Stanford alumni include the <a href="/wiki/Special_Olympics" title="Special Olympics">Special Olympics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tesla_Motors" title="Tesla Motors">Tesla Motors</a>, <a href="/wiki/LinkedIn" title="LinkedIn">LinkedIn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Varian_Associates" title="Varian Associates">Varian Associates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pandora_Radio" title="Pandora Radio">Pandora Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">Electronic Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trader_Joe%27s" title="Trader Joe's">Trader Joe's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Laboratories" title="Dolby Laboratories">Dolby Laboratories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Schwab" title="Charles Schwab" class="mw-redirect">Charles Schwab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_One" title="Capital One">Capital One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renren" title="Renren">Renren</a> (the Chinese version of <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>), <a href="/wiki/TechCrunch" title="TechCrunch">TechCrunch</a>, <a href="/wiki/IDEO" title="IDEO">IDEO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiva_(organization)" title="Kiva (organization)">Kiva.org</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acumen_Fund" title="Acumen Fund" class="mw-redirect">Acumen Fund</a>, <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret" title="Victoria's Secret">Victoria's Secret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Firefox" title="Firefox">Firefox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Match.com" title="Match.com">Match.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Participant_Media" title="Participant Media">Participant Media</a> and <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a>.</p> 
     <p>Former Japanese Prime Ministers <a href="/wiki/Yukio_Hatoyama" title="Yukio Hatoyama">Yukio Hatoyama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taro_Aso" title="Taro Aso" class="mw-redirect">Taro Aso</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup> former U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover" title="Herbert Hoover">Herbert Hoover</a>, former U.S. Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Warren_Christopher" title="Warren Christopher">Warren Christopher</a>, former Israeli Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ehud_Barak" title="Ehud Barak">Ehud Barak</a>, former Peruvian President <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Toledo" title="Alejandro Toledo">Alejandro Toledo</a>, former President of Guatemala <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Serrano_Elias" title="Jorge Serrano Elias" class="mw-redirect">Jorge Serrano Elias</a>, current President of the <a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Waheed_Hassan" title="Mohammed Waheed Hassan">Mohammed Waheed Hassan</a>, former Vice President of Iran <a href="/wiki/Mohammad-Reza_Aref" title="Mohammad-Reza Aref" class="mw-redirect">Mohammad-Reza Aref</a>, former Honduras President <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Maduro" title="Ricardo Maduro">Ricardo Maduro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philippe,_Duke_of_Brabant" title="Prince Philippe, Duke of Brabant">Prince Philippe, Duke of Brabant</a>, the Crown Prince of Belgium, are alumni. Former Ghanaian President <a href="/wiki/John_Atta_Mills" title="John Atta Mills">John Atta Mills</a> earned his J.D. as a <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Scholar" title="Fulbright Scholar" class="mw-redirect">Fulbright Scholar</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Law_School" title="Stanford Law School">Stanford Law School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> U.S. Supreme Court Justices <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Kennedy" title="Anthony Kennedy">Anthony Kennedy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Breyer" title="Stephen Breyer">Stephen Breyer</a> and former Justices <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Day_O%27Connor" title="Sandra Day O'Connor">Sandra Day O'Connor</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Rehnquist" title="William Rehnquist">William Rehnquist</a> are also alumni.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright">

     <p>Other alumni in politics include UN Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Susan_Rice" title="Susan Rice">Susan Rice</a>, former Secretary of Defense and current Stanford professor <a href="/wiki/William_Perry" title="William Perry">William Perry</a>, former US Ambassador to Afghanistan <a href="/wiki/Karl_Eikenberry" title="Karl Eikenberry">Karl Eikenberry</a>, Former US Ambassador to Mexico <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Pascual" title="Carlos Pascual">Carlos Pascual</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Donahoe" title="Eileen Donahoe">Eileen Donahoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Ambassador_to_the_United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United States Ambassador to the United Nations Human Rights Council">United States Ambassador to the United Nations Human Rights Council</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Kennard" title="William Kennard">William Kennard</a>, U.S. Ambassador to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_McFaul" title="Michael McFaul">Michael McFaul</a>, US Ambassador to Russia, Newark Mayor <a href="/wiki/Cory_Booker" title="Cory Booker">Cory Booker</a>, and current US Senators <a href="/wiki/Dianne_Feinstein" title="Dianne Feinstein">Dianne Feinstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Baucus" title="Max Baucus">Max Baucus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bingaman" title="Jeff Bingaman">Jeff Bingaman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Merkley" title="Jeff Merkley">Jeff Merkley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Wyden" title="Ron Wyden">Ron Wyden</a>, and Representatives <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Becerra" title="Xavier Becerra">Xavier Becerra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judy_Biggert" title="Judy Biggert">Judy Biggert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoe_Lofgren" title="Zoe Lofgren">Zoe Lofgren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Schiff" title="Adam Schiff">Adam Schiff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Sensenbrenner" title="Jim Sensenbrenner">Jim Sensenbrenner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Wu" title="David Wu">David Wu</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Clinton" title="Chelsea Clinton">Chelsea Clinton</a> attended Stanford while her <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">father</a> was President, and met her future husband while attending.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>NBA guard <a href="/wiki/Landry_Fields" title="Landry Fields">Landry Fields</a>, NBA centers <a href="/wiki/Brook_Lopez" title="Brook Lopez">Brook Lopez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Lopez" title="Robin Lopez">Robin Lopez</a>, NFL quarterbacks <a href="/wiki/Frankie_Albert" title="Frankie Albert">Frankie Albert</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Brodie" title="John Brodie">John Brodie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Plunkett" title="Jim Plunkett">Jim Plunkett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trent_Edwards" title="Trent Edwards">Trent Edwards</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Elway" title="John Elway">John Elway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Luck" title="Andrew Luck">Andrew Luck</a>, NFL receivers <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Banks_(American_football)" title="Gordon Banks (American football)">Gordon Banks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_McCaffrey" title="Ed McCaffrey">Ed McCaffrey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doug_Baldwin_(American_football)" title="Doug Baldwin (American football)">Doug Baldwin</a>, NFL Fullback <a href="/wiki/Jon_Ritchie" title="Jon Ritchie">Jon Ritchie</a>, runner <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Hall_(runner)" title="Ryan Hall (runner)">Ryan Hall</a>, MLB starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_Mussina" title="Mike Mussina">Mike Mussina</a>, MLB left-fielder <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Quentin" title="Carlos Quentin">Carlos Quentin</a>, MLB infielder <a href="/wiki/Jed_Lowrie" title="Jed Lowrie">Jed Lowrie</a>, MLB catcher <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Robinson_(baseball)" title="Bruce Robinson (baseball)" class="mw-redirect">Bruce Robinson</a>, Grand Slam winning tennis players <a href="/wiki/John_McEnroe" title="John McEnroe">John McEnroe</a> (did not graduate) (singles and doubles) and (doubles) <a href="/wiki/Bob_Bryan" title="Bob Bryan">Bob</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bryan" title="Mike Bryan">Mike Bryan</a>, professional golfers <a href="/wiki/Tom_Watson_(golfer)" title="Tom Watson (golfer)">Tom Watson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tiger_Woods" title="Tiger Woods">Tiger Woods</a> (did not graduate), <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Football" title="New Zealand Football">New Zealand Football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers" title="Queens Park Rangers" class="mw-redirect">Queens Park Rangers</a> Defender <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Nelsen" title="Ryan Nelsen">Ryan Nelsen</a>, Olympic swimmers <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Thompson" title="Jenny Thompson">Jenny Thompson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Summer_Sanders" title="Summer Sanders">Summer Sanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Morales" title="Pablo Morales">Pablo Morales</a>, Olympic figure skater <a href="/wiki/Debi_Thomas" title="Debi Thomas">Debi Thomas</a>, Olympic gymnast <a href="/wiki/Amy_Chow" title="Amy Chow">Amy Chow</a>, Olympic and World Cup soccer players <a href="/wiki/Julie_Foudy" title="Julie Foudy">Julie Foudy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Rafanelli" title="Sarah Rafanelli">Sarah Rafanelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelley_O%27Hara" title="Kelley O'Hara">Kelley O'Hara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christen_Press" title="Christen Press">Christen Press</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Barnhart" title="Nicole Barnhart">Nicole Barnhart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Buehler" title="Rachel Buehler">Rachel Buehler</a>, Olympic water polo players <a href="/wiki/Tony_Azevedo" title="Tony Azevedo">Tony Azevedo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Villa" title="Brenda Villa">Brenda Villa</a>, Olympic softball player <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Mendoza" title="Jessica Mendoza">Jessica Mendoza</a>, Olympic volleyball player <a href="/wiki/Kerri_Walsh" title="Kerri Walsh" class="mw-redirect">Kerri Walsh</a>, Olympic volleyball player <a href="/wiki/Logan_Tom" title="Logan Tom">Logan Tom</a>, and Heisman finalist <a href="/wiki/Toby_Gerhart" title="Toby Gerhart">Toby Gerhart</a> are alumni.</p> 
     <p>In the field of entertainment, <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Connelly" title="Jennifer Connelly">Jennifer Connelly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Koppel" title="Ted Koppel">Ted Koppel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Savage" title="Ben Savage">Ben Savage</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tablo" title="Tablo">Tablo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Maddow" title="Rachel Maddow">Rachel Maddow</a> are prominent graduates. Other alumni include <a href="/wiki/Jay_Roach" title="Jay Roach">Jay Roach</a>, director of the <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers_(film_series)" title="Austin Powers (film series)">Austin Powers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Parents" title="Meet the Parents">Meet the Parents</a></i> films and <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Change_(film)" title="Game Change (film)">Game Change</a></i>, among others. <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Payne" title="Alexander Payne">Alexander Payne</a> wrote and directed such films as <i><a href="/wiki/Sideways" title="Sideways">Sideways</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Descendants" title="The Descendants">The Descendants</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/About_Schmidt" title="About Schmidt">About Schmidt</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/David_Chase" title="David Chase">David Chase</a>, a seven-time Emmy Award winner, is best known as the creator and writer of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sopranos" title="The Sopranos">The Sopranos</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/John_Steinbeck" title="John Steinbeck">John Steinbeck</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/Of_Mice_and_Men" title="Of Mice and Men">Of Mice and Men</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Grapes_of_Wrath" title="The Grapes of Wrath">The Grapes of Wrath</a></i>, attended Stanford for five years but did not receive a degree. <a href="/wiki/Ken_Kesey" title="Ken Kesey">Ken Kesey</a> studied creative writing at Stanford, and began the manuscript of <i><a href="/wiki/One_Flew_Over_the_Cuckoo%27s_Nest_(novel)" title="One Flew Over the Cuckoo's Nest (novel)">One Flew Over the Cuckoo's Nest</a></i> while attending. <a href="/wiki/Larry_McMurtry" title="Larry McMurtry">Larry McMurtry</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/Lonesome_Dove" title="Lonesome Dove">Lonesome Dove</a></i>, studied for two years at Stanford on the <a href="/wiki/Stegner_Fellowship" title="Stegner Fellowship">Stegner Fellowship</a>. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cunningham" title="Michael Cunningham">Michael Cunningham</a> is best known as author of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hours_(novel)" title="The Hours (novel)">The Hours</a></i>, while <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Eugenides" title="Jeffrey Eugenides">Jeffrey Eugenides</a> wrote <i><a href="/wiki/Middlesex" title="Middlesex">Middlesex</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Virgin_Suicides" title="The Virgin Suicides">The Virgin Suicides</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/N._Scott_Momaday" title="N. Scott Momaday">N. Scott Momaday</a> is widely credited as a leader in bringing Native American fiction into mainstream American literature. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Poet_Laureate" title="United States Poet Laureate">U.S. Poet Laureates</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Pinsky" title="Robert Pinsky">Robert Pinsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hass" title="Robert Hass">Robert Hass</a> were classmates while attaining their Ph.D.s at Stanford, and another Poet Laureate, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Levine_(poet)" title="Philip Levine (poet)">Philip Levine</a>, studied poetry at Stanford. Other prominent novelists and poets have been recipients of the renowned Stegner Fellowship in fiction and poetry.</p> 
     <p>Former <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> president Derek Bok; the president of <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Levin" title="Rick Levin">Rick Levin</a>; and the provost of Yale, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Salovey" title="Peter Salovey">Peter Salovey</a> earned a bachelor's degree at Stanford, while the presidents of <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caltech" title="Caltech" class="mw-redirect">Caltech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Reif" title="Rafael Reif" class="mw-redirect">Rafael Reif</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Lou_Chameau" title="Jean-Lou Chameau">Jean-Lou Chameau</a>, respectively, earned <a href="/wiki/Ph.D." title="Ph.D." class="mw-redirect">Ph.D.s</a> there. Alan M. Garber, the current Provost of Harvard, earned his M.D. from <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Medical_School" title="Stanford Medical School" class="mw-redirect">Stanford Medical School</a>. Other University presidents include <a href="/wiki/William_Brody" title="William Brody" class="mw-redirect">William Brody</a>, former president of <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Johns Hopkins University">Johns Hopkins</a>, Vartan Gregorian, former president of <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_P._Leahy" title="William P. Leahy">William P. Leahy</a>, president of <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>. At least eight Stanford alumni have won the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_prize" title="Nobel prize" class="mw-redirect">Nobel prize</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Stanford_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
      <ol class="references"> 
       <li id="cite_note-noteLargest-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-noteLargest_8-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It is often claimed that Stanford has the largest contiguous campus in the world (or the United States)<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> but that depends on definitions. <a href="/wiki/Berry_College" title="Berry College">Berry College</a> with over 26,000 acres (11,000&nbsp;ha), <a href="/wiki/Paul_Smith%27s_College" title="Paul Smith's College">Paul Smith's College</a> with 14,200 acres (5,700&nbsp;ha), and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a> with 18,500 acres (7,500&nbsp;ha) are larger but are not usually classified as <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">universities</a>. <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a> at 8,610 acres (3,480&nbsp;ha) has more land but it is not contiguous. However the <a href="/wiki/Sewanee:_The_University_of_the_South" title="Sewanee: The University of the South">University of the South</a> has over 13,000 acres (5,300&nbsp;ha).</span></li> 
       <li id="cite_note-noteStanfordRanch-28"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-noteStanfordRanch_28-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to the main campus of 8,180 acres (3,310&nbsp;ha) from the Palo Alto Farm, the university was originally endowed with the Vina Ranch of 59,000 acres (24,000&nbsp;ha) near <a href="/wiki/Vina,_California" title="Vina, California">Vina</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tehama_County" title="Tehama County" class="mw-redirect">Tehama County</a> and the Gridley farm of 22,000 acres (8,900&nbsp;ha) in <a href="/wiki/Butte_County,_California" title="Butte County, California">Butte County</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Unlike the Palo Alto Farm, these lands could be sold and later were. The Vina Ranch was sold in 1918 and the core part is now the Trappist <a href="/wiki/Abbey_of_New_Clairvaux" title="Abbey of New Clairvaux">Abbey of New Clairvaux</a>. The Gridley farm was originally part of <a href="/wiki/Rancho_Esquon" title="Rancho Esquon">Rancho Esquon</a>.</span></li> 
      </ol> 
     </div>

      <li>Rebecca S. Lowen, R. S. Lowen, <i>Creating the Cold War University: The Transformation of Stanford</i>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Press" title="University of California Press">University of California Press</a> 1997</li>
